## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task involves finding the stress-strain-temperature relationship for a material. Stress typically depends on strain through elastic/plastic constitutive laws, while temperature modifies material stiffness and strength through thermal softening mechanisms.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = c0 * (c1 - T) * epsilon (linear elasticity with linearly decreasing modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (exponential): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus with exponential thermal softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear stress-strain, e.g., Ramberg-Osgood inverse)
- Power-law with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (strain hardening with Arrhenius-type thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook type model: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Johnson-Cook with homologous temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * (1 - c2 * T**c3) (power-law hardening with power-law thermal softening)
- Arrhenius-type flow stress: sigma = c0 * sinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (hyperbolic sine creep/flow law)
- Polynomial stress-strain: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (nonlinear elastic with higher-order terms)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Thermal softening with rational form: sigma = c0 * epsilon / (1 + c1 * epsilon) * (c2 - T) (saturation hardening with linear thermal factor)
- Combined linear model: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T + c2 * epsilon * T (bilinear with coupling term)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 * log(1 + c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 * T) (logarithmic strain hardening with thermal softening)
- Generalized constitutive: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear thermal softening → Stress multiplied by factor (c0 - c1*T) or (1 - c0*T**c1), representing decreasing elastic modulus or yield strength with temperature
- Arrhenius thermal activation → exp(c0/T) or exp(c0*T) terms represent thermally activated deformation mechanisms (diffusion, dislocation climb)
- Strain hardening saturation → Terms like (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or epsilon/(1+c*epsilon) represent dislocation density saturation during plastic deformation
- Hyperbolic sine flow law → sinh(c*sigma) or sinh(c*epsilon) bridges power-law creep at low stress and exponential creep at high stress
- Multiplicative decomposition → Stress = f(epsilon) * g(T): separable strain hardening and thermal softening functions, common in Johnson-Cook type models
- Strain-temperature coupling → Product terms epsilon*T indicate that hardening rate itself depends on temperature, not just a multiplicative factor
- Phase transition discontinuity → Abrupt change in constitutive behavior at critical temperature suggests piecewise or sigmoidal temperature dependence
- Elastic-plastic transition → Combination of linear (elastic) and power-law (plastic) terms: c0*epsilon + c1*epsilon**c2 for bilinear-like behavior
